[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — LJE   139 

[2:0:189,29] 0820   Department of Justice - Continued 

[3:0:66,83] business entities who apply for state gambling licenses and monitoring the conduct of these licensees to ensure compliance  

[3:1:66,93] with the Gambling Control Act and applicable regulations. The Bureau’s Special Agents conduct criminal investigations in and  

[3:2:66,103] around tribal casinos and California cardrooms. In addition, the Bureau conducts audits and reviews for tribal gaming to ensure  

[3:3:66,113] that each tribe is in compliance with all aspects of the state gaming compact.  

[4:0:66,131] The Bureau of Investigation is the premiere investigative bureau that is responsible for investigating and dismantling criminal  

[4:1:66,141] organizations, as well as assisting with the prosecution of serious criminal offenses which present a significant and multi-

[4:2:66,152] jurisdictional threat to California. The Bureau prioritizes investigations related to transnational criminal organizations involved in  

[4:3:66,162] gangs, as well as cases involving environmental crimes, public corruption, major white-collar fraud, underground economy,  

[4:4:66,172] recycle fraud, foreign prosecution, human trafficking and sexual predator apprehension crimes. In addition, the Bureau serves a  

[4:5:66,182] principal role in providing leadership, coordination, and support to law enforcement through multi-agency drug, gang and major  

[4:6:66,192] crimes task forces statewide.  

[5:0:66,210] The Office of the Chief enhances public safety by providing training, technical, and administrative support to the investigative,  

[5:1:66,220] regulatory and forensic components of the Division of Law Enforcement and other criminal justice agencies. The Office serves  

[5:2:66,230] as the policy-making and oversight body for its four operational bureaus.  

[6:0:66,248] 0445 - CALIFORNIA JUSTICE INFORMATION SERVICES  

[7:0:66,269] The California Justice Information Services Division provides criminal justice intelligence, information, and identification  

[7:1:66,279] services to law enforcement, regulatory agencies, and the public. Five major functional areas carry out these primary services:  

[7:2:66,289] 1) The Bureau of Criminal Identification & Investigative Services consolidates the identification, investigative, and field services  

[7:3:66,299] functions, providing information and technical assistance on manual and automated systems including the fingerprint  

[8:0:66,309] identification system and the violent crime information system; 2) The Bureau of Criminal Information and Analysis consolidates  

[8:1:66,320] the functions related to the authorization, release, and use of criminal offender record information for law enforcement  

[8:2:66,330] investigatory and regulatory purposes; 3) The Hawkins Data Center operates the Criminal Justice Information System and the  

[8:3:66,340] California Law Enforcement Telecommunications System, as well as provides IT services for the Attorney General’s Office; 4)  

[8:4:66,350] the Operations Support Program provides business resumption planning and administrative support and oversight; and 5) the  

[8:5:66,360] Department of Justice Research Center, within the Operations Support Program, oversees statistical models and engages in  

[8:6:66,371] the analysis of data to provide evidence-based research.  

[9:0:66,388] 9900 - DIRECTORATE AND ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,409] The Directorate and the Administration Division of the Department of Justice consists of the Division of Operations and the  

[10:1:66,419] Attorney General's Executive Office. The Executive Office maintains the overall direction and administration of the diverse  

[10:2:66,429] programs and projects of the department, including the Equal Employment Rights and Resolution Office, the Office of Program  

[10:3:66,439] Oversight and Accountability, the Opinions Unit, the Solicitor General's Unit, the Office of Legislative Affairs, the Office of  

[10:4:66,449] Communications and the Public Inquiry Unit. In addition, the Division of Operations provides support functions essential to the  

[10:5:66,460] department's operations, including fiscal, personnel, and specialized services such as legal secretarial support, litigation  

[10:6:66,470] support, and legal case management services.

[3:0:242,112] 0840   State Controller  

[4:0:66,134] The State Controller is the chief fiscal officer of California, the fifth largest economy in the world. Principally responsible for  

[4:1:66,144] transparency and accountability of the state's financial resources, the Controller ensures the appropriate disbursement and  

[4:2:66,154] tracking of taxpayer dollars. The Controller serves on dozens of state boards, commissions, and committees with  

[4:3:66,164] duties   ranging from   administrative oversight of the nation's two largest public pension funds,   to protection of state lands and  

[4:4:66,175] coastlines,   to modernization and financing of major infrastructure. The Controller also offers fiscal guidance to local  

[4:5:66,185] governments and has independent auditing authority over government agencies related to the spending of state funds. The  

[4:6:66,195] Controller's primary objectives are to:  

[5:0:65,213] • Account for and control disbursement of all state funds, issuing warrants in payment of the state's bills, including lottery  

[5:1:76,223] prizes.  

[6:0:65,239] • Determine legality and accuracy of financial claims against the state.  

[6:1:65,255] • Audit state and local government programs and agencies.  

[7:0:65,271] • Safeguard many types of assets until claimed by the rightful owners, in accordance with the Unclaimed Property Law.  

[7:1:65,288] • Inform the public of the state's financial condition.  

[8:0:65,304] • Inform the public of financial transactions of city, county, and other local governments.  

[8:1:65,320] • Administer the Uniform State Payroll System.  

[9:0:65,336] • Audit and process all personnel and payroll transactions for state civil service, state exempt employees, California State  

[9:1:76,346] University employees, and Judicial Council employees.

[9:0:66,551] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:1:66,570] 0500100 - ACCOUNTING AND REPORTING  

[10:0:66,591] The State Accounting and Reporting Division maintains uniform and systematic control accounts of all receipts, payments,  

[10:1:66,601] state fund balances, and bonded indebtedness; reports the financial condition of the state; monitors the cash flow of the  

[10:2:66,611] General Fund; administers the statewide discharge from accountability program; participates in offsetting monies owed to the  

[10:3:66,621] state; and collaborates with the Department of Finance, the Treasurer, and the Department of General Services to develop and  

[10:4:66,631] implement the Financial Information System for California (FI$Cal) to ensure the system meets the state's primary objectives  

[10:5:66,642] and provides best business practices for the state.  

[11:0:66,662] The Local Government Programs and Services Division maintains a database of information and reports on local financial  

[11:1:66,672] transactions and government compensation; apportions shared revenues to local governments; administers local mandated  

[11:2:66,682] cost programs; approves county cost allocation plans; prescribes uniform accounting procedures for counties, special districts,  

[11:3:66,693] and trial court revenues; administers and collects estate and inheritance taxes; collects delinquent insurance and motor vehicle  

[11:4:66,703] fuel taxes, petroleum and gas assessments, and trial court penalties; refunds gasoline taxes paid on fuel consumed for off-

[11:5:66,713] highway purposes; instructs and advises county tax collectors; approves state and local government requests to participate in

[3:0:66,83] the Interagency Intercept Collection Program; and administers the Property Tax Postponement Program for seniors and people

[3:2:66,111] 0500200 - AUDITS  

[4:0:66,131] The Audits Division determines the legality and accuracy of all claims against the state through the performance of prepayment  

[4:1:66,141] audits; assures the accuracy of local government claims and financial statements submitted to the state and federal  

[4:2:66,152] governments by establishing and updating audit guidelines, and reviewing audits performed by independent auditors; performs  

[4:3:66,162] field audits for state and federal programs; reviews the single audit reports of local governments and local education agencies  

[4:4:66,172] that receive pass-through federal funds from state agencies; and audits major businesses for compliance with the Unclaimed  

[4:5:66,182] Property Law.  

[5:0:66,200] 0500300 - PERSONNEL AND PAYROLL SERVICES  

[6:0:66,220] The Personnel and Payroll Services Division administers the state's payroll, employment history, the automated travel expense  

[6:1:66,230] reimbursement system, and leave accounting processes.   The Division works with   the Department of Human Resources,  

[6:2:66,241] California Public Employees' Retirement System, Judicial Council, Department of Finance, and California State University  

[6:3:66,251] Chancellor's Office to maximize the efficiency of the state's personnel and payroll functions.  

[7:0:66,271] The California State Payroll System Project was initiated to modernize the statewide human resource management and  

[7:1:66,281] payroll   systems as part of a fully integrated solution. The system should enable the state to improve management processes  

[7:2:66,292] and fulfill its payroll, reporting, and deduction processing obligations accurately and on time.  

[7:3:66,309] 0500400 - UNCLAIMED PROPERTY  

[8:0:66,330] The Unclaimed Property Division administers the Unclaimed Property Law by providing one central source for owners to claim  

[8:1:66,340] their property; notifying owners of their unclaimed property before it is transferred to the state; receiving unclaimed property  

[8:2:66,350] from banks, savings and loans, insurance companies,   and other businesses; and providing outreach and education for  

[8:3:66,360] businesses holding unclaimed property.  

[8:4:66,378] 0500500 - DISBURSEMENTS  

[9:0:66,398] The Disbursements Bureau produces and delivers all payments of the state's obligations after auditing and clearance through  

[9:1:66,409] control accounts.   Examples of some of the state's payments are personal income tax refunds, payroll, vendor payments,   and  

[9:2:66,419] retirement payments. Disbursements also provides post-issuance services including disposition of undeliverable warrants; lost  

[9:3:66,429] warrant duplication; and maintenance and production of paid warrant images.  

[9:4:66,447] 0500900 - DEPARTMENTAL ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,467] The Executive Office and the Administration Program provide executive direction and support services to all   divisions in the  

[10:1:66,477] State Controller's Office. The Information Systems Division develops, maintains, and operates all of the department's  

[10:2:66,488] mainframe, client-server, and web-based systems; and oversees the planning, procurement, use, and maintenance of  

[10:3:66,498] information technology hardware and software.

[10:0:216,459] 0845   Department of Insurance  

[11:0:66,480] California's publicly-elected Insurance Commissioner regulates the fourth largest insurance economy in the world with insurers  

[11:1:66,490] collecting more than $310 billion in premiums annually in California while protecting consumers and the integrity, health and  

[11:2:66,501] vitality of the insurance marketplace. The vision of the California Department of Insurance (CDI) is "Insurance Protection for All  

[11:3:66,511] Californians." CDI accomplishes this by enforcing insurance laws and regulations, assisting consumers in their dealings with  

[11:4:66,521] insurers, and using innovation to improve services for insurance producers and consumers.  

[12:0:66,539] The CDI licenses and regulates insurance companies, and individuals in California. Currently, the CDI oversees and licenses  

[12:1:66,549] approximately 1,400 insurance companies and approximately 420,000 individuals and business entities as insurance agents,  

[12:2:66,559] brokers, adjusters and bail agents. Additionally, the CDI receives and investigates approximately 200,000 consumer inquiries  

[12:3:66,569] and complaints annually; performs examinations to ensure the financial solvency of companies; receives more than  

[12:4:66,579] approximately 23,000 suspected fraudulent claim referrals annually; receives and reviews approximately 6,800 rate filing  

[12:5:66,590] applications annually; and works in conjunction with local, state and federal law enforcement agencies to investigate and  

[12:6:66,600] prosecute fraudulent insurance practices.

[13:0:66,460] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[13:1:65,480] • Enhanced Fraud Investigation and Prevention (Fraud Data Analytics/eDiscovery)—The Budget includes $840,000 General  

[13:2:76,490] Fund to support the Fraud Data Analytics Software (FDAS) system and the eDiscovery Software-as-a-Service solution,  

[13:3:76,500] which are currently used by the Fraud Division within the California Department of Insurance to perform fraud investigations  

[13:4:76,510] of civil whistleblower cases related to the California Insurance Fraud Prevention Act, Insurance Code section 1871.7, et seq.  

[13:5:76,520] Updates to the algorithms of the FDAS system will help the Fraud Division continue to select cases with the greatest impact  

[13:6:76,531] on the industry and/or cases that have the greatest potential to benefit California consumers, while remaining relevant as  

[13:7:76,541] fraud patterns change. The renewal of the eDiscovery software reduces the time spent on processing, reviewing, and  

[13:8:76,551] organizing discovery data, which provides attorneys the ability to initiate independent investigations into large scale  

[13:9:76,561] fraudulent schemes.  

[14:0:65,577] • Workers' Compensation Fraud Program—The Budget includes $3.4 million Insurance Fund to support workers’  

[14:1:76,588] compensation fraud investigation and prosecution workload increases, which aligns with the increased assessment  

[14:2:76,598] approved by the Fraud Assessment Commission in September 2019. The goal of this program is to arrest, prosecute, and  

[14:3:76,608] convict perpetrators who commit workers’ compensation insurance fraud and to provide anti-fraud outreach and training to  

[14:4:76,618] the public, private, and governmental sectors.

[8:0:66,415] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:0:66,434] 0520 - REGULATION OF INSURANCE COMPANIES AND INSURANCE PRODUCERS  

[10:0:66,452] The objectives of this program are to: (1) prevent losses to policyholders, beneficiaries or the public due to the insolvency of  

[10:1:66,462] insurers, including the review of complex, principles-based reserving methods to avoid reliance on black box models; (2)  

[10:2:66,472] prevent unlawful or unfair practices by insurers as defined by the Insurance Code; (3) ensure that property and casualty  

[10:3:66,482] insurance rates are not excessive, inadequate, unfairly discriminatory or otherwise in violation of the Insurance Code and the  

[10:4:66,493] California Code of Regulations; (4) assess and implement strategies to reduce climate risk impacts in the insurance sector; (5)  

[10:5:66,503] review health insurance rates filed with CDI to determine whether they are reasonable and attempt to get unreasonable rates  

[10:6:66,513] lowered by insurers; and (6) ensure that applicants for insurance licenses, and holders of insurance licenses, satisfy and  

[10:7:66,523] maintain the qualifications for licensure. Through the Conservation and Liquidation Office, the CDI administers the estates of  

[10:8:66,533] insolvent and delinquent insurance companies.  

[10:9:66,551] 0525 - CONSUMER PROTECTION  

[11:0:66,571] The objectives of this program are to: (1) provide direct service to California consumers by protecting insurance policyholders  

[11:1:66,582] and other parties involved in insurance transactions against unfair or illegal practices with respect to claims handling, rating or  

[11:2:66,592] underwriting by insurers and (2) protect applicants and policyholders from discriminatory, unlawful or fraudulent practices or  

[11:3:66,602] incompetence relating to the sale of insurance and (3) oversee programs that benefit California's underserved communities.  

[11:4:66,620] 0530 - FRAUD CONTROL  

[12:0:66,637] The objective of this program is to protect the public from economic loss by actively investigating, arresting and referring for  

[12:1:66,648] prosecution or adjudication those who commit insurance fraud and other violations of the law. The program is primarily staffed  

[12:2:66,658] by sworn peace officers who conduct criminal investigations of insurance fraud and related criminal cases. The program  

[12:3:66,668] administers the Insurance Frauds Prevention Act (IFPA), which authorizes the department to conduct criminal insurance fraud  

[12:4:66,678] investigations. In addition, the IFPA authorizes the Commissioner to initiate or intervene in whistle-blower "qui tam" actions  

[12:5:66,688] seeking civil penalties against perpetrators of insurance fraud.  

[12:6:66,706] 0535 - GENERAL FUND TAX COLLECTION AND COMPLIANCE  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[8:0:183,450] 0850   California State Lottery Commission  

[9:0:66,471] In 1984, Proposition 37 amended the California Constitution to authorize the establishment of a statewide lottery. As an  

[9:1:66,481] initiative statute, the California State Lottery Act (Act) of 1984 created the California State Lottery Commission and gave it  

[9:2:66,492] broad powers to oversee the operations of a statewide lottery. The purpose of the Act was to provide supplemental monies to  

[9:3:66,502] benefit public education. The Lottery is overseen by a five-person Commission appointed by the Governor and confirmed by  

[9:4:66,512] the State Senate.  

[10:0:66,532] The Act initially required that 50 percent of total annual revenues be returned to the public in the form of prizes and at least 34  

[10:1:66,543] percent of total revenues be allocated to the benefit of public education. No more than 16 percent of total revenues were to be  

[10:2:66,553] used for administrative costs.  

[11:0:66,573] In 2010, the Act was changed to allow the Lottery flexibility to pay out more money in prizes and reduce the administrative cost  

[11:1:66,583] limit to 13 percent of total revenues. Along with that flexibility, the new law requires the Lottery to meet minimum levels of  

[11:2:66,594] contribution to public education. Revenues to education are placed in a special fund, known as the California State Lottery  

[11:3:66,604] Education Fund, which holds revenues until they are allocated on a per capita basis, using prior year certified Average Daily  

[11:4:66,614] Attendance data, to the following categories: K-12 education, Community Colleges, the California State University, the  

[11:5:66,624] University of California, and other educational entities, including the California Schools for the Deaf and Blind.  

[12:0:66,645] In the 34 years since sales began in October 1985 through June 30, 2019, the California State Lottery has raised $36.0 billion  

[12:1:66,655] for public education, including $1.85 billion in FY 2018-19.  

[13:0:66,675] Because of the inherently variable nature of lottery ticket sales, revenue estimates for 2019-20 and 2020-21 cannot be made  

[13:1:66,685] with certainty.

[1:0:169,53] 0855   California Gambling Control Commission  

[2:0:66,75] The mission of the California Gambling Control Commission (Commission) is to ensure integrity in California's gaming  

[2:1:66,85] environment. The Commission has jurisdiction over gambling establishments (cardrooms), third-party providers of proposition  

[2:2:66,95] player services, and certain aspects of Tribal casinos, pursuant to its authority under state law and Tribal-State Gaming  

[2:3:66,105] Compacts (Compacts). The Commission also has jurisdiction over gaming policies, regulations, criteria, and standards.  

[3:0:66,126] There are 86 licensed cardrooms in California over which the Commission has broad regulatory and adjudicatory authority. This  

[3:1:66,136] authority extends to the operation, concentration, and supervision of the cardrooms and all persons and things related to each  

[3:2:66,146] licensed establishment.  

[4:0:66,167] The Commission has fiduciary, regulatory, and administrative responsibilities related to Tribal gaming that include: (1)  

[4:1:66,177] distributing specified Tribal gaming revenues to Non-Compact, Non-Gaming and Limited-Gaming Tribes; (2) making suitability  

[4:2:66,187] determinations for key employees, gaming resource suppliers, and financial sources; and (3) serving as the administrator of the  

[4:3:66,197] Indian Gaming Revenue Sharing Trust Fund, Indian Gaming Special Distribution Fund, and the Tribal Nation Grant Fund.

[10:0:209,561] 0860   State Board of Equalization  

[11:0:66,583] The State Board of Equalization's (BOE)   duties   primarily include assessing and allocating the property values of railroads and  

[11:1:66,593] specified utilities and businesses; adjudicating property tax appeals of taxable government owned property; overseeing the  

[11:2:66,603] property tax assessment practices of the 58 county assessors; adopting rules to clarify property tax laws; and administering the  

[11:3:66,614] alcoholic beverage excise tax and the insurance tax, including appeals. The BOE contracts with the   California Department of  

[11:4:66,624] Tax and Fee Administration (CDTFA)   to administer the alcoholic beverage tax and insurance tax program.

[6:0:66,304] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,324] 0570025 - COUNTY ASSESSMENT STANDARDS PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,341] This program ensures that taxable properties are enrolled and assessed by the 58 county assessors in full conformity with the  

[7:1:66,352] law. The BOE is also charged with providing consultation and services to the county assessors and their staff, establishing  

[7:2:66,362] standards, providing training for assessors and assessment appeals boards, evaluating the effectiveness of each county  

[7:3:66,372] assessor's administration, co-administering the welfare exemption, and administering the Legal Entity Ownership Program.  

[7:4:66,390] 0570050 - STATE-ASSESSED PROPERTY PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,410] This program   values and assesses   inter-county pipelines and properties owned or used by railroads, regulated telephone  

[8:1:66,420] companies, companies transmitting or selling gas or electricity, and private railroad car companies. Local jurisdictions use the  

[8:2:66,430] established values for the levy and collection of local property taxes. In addition, the BOE collects the Private Railroad Car Tax  

[8:3:66,441] that is deposited in the state General Fund.  

[8:4:66,458] 0570150 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE TAX PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,479] This program collects the excise tax imposed on the sale, distribution, or importation of alcoholic beverages in California. The  

[9:1:66,489] BOE contracts with the CDTFA to administer this program.  

[9:2:66,507] 0570575 - INSURANCE TAX PROGRAM  

[10:0:66,527] This program provides revenue to the Insurance Tax Fund. Revenue is generated from taxes assessed on insurance  

[10:1:66,537] premiums, underwriting profits from ocean marine insurance, and retaliatory assessments levied on   out-of-state insurers. The  

[10:2:66,547] taxes collected are used to pay refunds or transferred to the General Fund. The BOE contracts with the CDTFA to administer  

[10:3:66,558] this program.

[7:0:226,282] 0870   Office of Tax Appeals  

[7:1:66,303] The Office of Tax Appeals (OTA) was established effective January 1, 2018, by Chapter 16, Statutes of 2017 (AB 102). The  

[7:2:66,313] OTA performs those tax appeal duties formerly assigned by statute to the State Board of Equalization, including personal  

[7:3:66,324] income tax appeals, franchise tax appeals, and sales and use tax appeals. The OTA's mission is to ensure tax appeals are  

[7:4:66,334] performed in a fair, transparent, consistent, equitable, and impartial manner.  

[8:0:66,354] The OTA has hearing offices in Sacramento, Fresno, and Los Angeles.

[8:0:66,364] The Administration Division ensures the efficient operation of the OTA by providing fiscal oversight and performing personnel

[8:2:66,392] 0620300 - HEARINGS DIVISION  

[9:0:66,413] The Hearings Division is responsible for hearing and determining tax appeals arising from taxpayer disputes from assessments  

[9:1:66,423] made by the Franchise Tax Board and the Department of Tax and Fee Administration.   It is   responsible for writing and  

[9:2:66,433] publishing decisions for each case that comes before OTA.  

[9:3:66,451] 0620400 - FOUNDATIONS   DIVISION  

[10:0:66,469] The   Foundations Division is responsible for preparing and developing cases for Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) determination.  

[10:1:66,479] They are subject matter experts in tax law who use their expertise to expedite the ALJ determination process.

[6:0:236,216] 0890   Secretary of State  

[7:0:66,237] The Secretary of State, a constitutionally established office, is the chief elections officer of the state and is responsible for the  

[7:1:66,247] administration and enforcement of election laws. The Office also is responsible for administering and enforcing laws pertaining  

[7:2:66,258] to filing documents associated with corporations, limited liability companies, partnerships, limited partnerships, unincorporated  

[7:3:66,268] associations and pertaining to filing bonds and perfecting security agreements. In addition, the Office is responsible for  

[7:4:66,278] commissioning notaries public, enforcing the notary laws, and in conjunction with being the home of the State Archives,  

[8:0:66,288] administering a state records management program and preserving documents and records having historical significance. The  

[8:1:66,298] Secretary of State is the filing officer for lobbying and campaign registration and disclosure documents filed under the Political  

[8:2:66,309] Reform Act. The Secretary of State also operates the Safe at Home program, maintains the Domestic Partners and Advance  

[8:3:66,319] Health Care Directives registries, provides support functions for the Voting Modernization Board, and is home to the California  

[8:4:66,329] Museum.  

[9:0:66,349] Policy associated with the administration of the Office is accomplished through the divisions of Elections, Political Reform,  

[9:1:66,360] Business Programs, Archives, Information Technology, and Management Services.

[3:1:66,93] agricultural liens, and equipment liens are also filed in Uniform Commercial Code, as well as notices of various tax liens  

[3:2:66,103] submitted by state and federal taxing agencies such as the Franchise Tax Board and the Internal Revenue Service.  

[4:0:66,124] Notary Public and Special Filings appoints and commissions qualified notaries public for four- year terms, reviews and  

[5:0:66,134] approves notary public education courses, and certifies to the authenticity of signatures of notaries public and public officials on  

[5:1:66,144] documents for use in foreign countries. Special Filings include trademarks and service marks as well as surety bonds that  

[5:2:66,154] certain business entities are required to file, notices of joint power agreements, city and county charters, and claims for  

[5:3:66,164] successor-in-interest. This area also has disciplinary functions with regard to notaries public and immigration consultants.  

[6:0:66,185] The Advance Health Care Directive (AHCD) Registry maintains AHCDs, which allow a person to indicate his/her medical  

[6:1:66,195] treatment preferences if he/she cannot speak or make decisions for him/herself. The AHCD also may designate someone else  

[6:2:66,205] to make decisions regarding medical treatment. AHCDs and related information can be provided upon request to the  

[6:3:66,215] registrant's health care provider, public guardian, or legal representative.  

[7:0:66,236] The Domestic Partners Registry registers same-sex couples regardless of the age of the partners, and opposite-sex couples in  

[7:1:66,246] which one partner is at least 62 years old, as domestic partners in California.  

[8:0:66,266] The Victims of Corporate Fraud Compensation Fund provides limited restitution to victims of corporate fraud who are unable to  

[8:1:66,277] collect through other means on a judgment against a corporation for corporate fraud.  

[9:0:66,294] Safe at Home is a confidential mail forwarding program designed to assist victims and survivors of domestic violence and  

[9:1:66,305] human trafficking, sexual assault, stalking, elder/dependent adult abuse, their household members and minor children, and  

[9:2:66,315] reproductive healthcare employees, patients, and volunteers. Participants in the Safe at Home program are provided with a  

[9:3:66,325] free post office box to use as a substitute mailing address, thereby reducing or eliminating the need to use their actual  

[9:4:66,335] residential address. Once enrolled into the program, Safe at Home serves as a liaison for those participants who qualify for  

[9:5:66,345] additional confidential services offered by various state and local agencies.  

[10:0:66,363] 0705 - ELECTIONS  

[11:0:66,383] The Secretary of State serves as California’s chief elections officer and has broad responsibility to administer and oversee  

[11:1:66,394] federal and state elections held within California. The Elections Program maintains the official statewide database of registered  

[11:2:66,404] voters, tracks and certifies ballot measures, certifies candidates for placement on the ballot, and certifies official election  

[11:3:66,414] results. In addition, the program oversees the certification and modernization of voting equipment and the enhancement of  

[11:4:66,424] election processes. The program works to increase accessibility to voters, provides resources to educate voters on the  

[11:5:66,434] electoral system, and investigates election related criminal violations as provided by the California Elections Code.  

[12:0:66,455] This program includes the campaign and lobbying registration and disclosure provisions of the Political Reform Act of 1974.  

[12:1:66,465] Under this law, the Office registers all levels of campaign committees, and reviews for compliance with statutory requirements  

[12:2:66,475] all state-level candidate and campaign recipient committees, major donors, slate mailer, political party, and independent  

[12:3:66,485] expenditure committees. The program registers lobbyists (including placement agents), lobbying firms and lobbyist employers,  

[12:4:66,496] reviews for compliance with statutory requirements the periodic financial disclosure reports filed by lobbying entities, and  

[12:5:66,506] publishes a Lobbying Directory on the Internet. This program also supports the electronic filing requirements of the Political  

[12:6:66,516] Reform Act and posts relevant registration and disclosure information to the Office's web site so the public can track where  

[12:7:66,526] campaign money is raised and spent and what lobbying activity is occurring in state government. A searchable database of  

[12:8:66,536] campaign and lobbying financial activity is also provided through the web site.  

[13:0:66,554] 0710 - ARCHIVES  

[14:0:66,572] The California State Archives establishes and administers a records management program that applies efficient and  

[14:1:66,582] economical management methods to the creation, utilization, maintenance, retention, preservation, and disposal of state  

[14:2:66,592] records and acquires, indexes, preserves, and provides reference access to irreplaceable historic materials from the three  

[14:3:66,602] branches of state government. The Archives acquires physical and electronic records with legal, administrative or evidentiary  

[14:4:66,613] value, or that have historical significance. Materials are transferred to the Archives for permanent preservation.  

[15:0:66,630] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[16:0:66,651] This program develops and manages overall policy. It serves as the liaison to other state agencies, the Legislature, the federal  

[16:1:66,661] government, and other states' Secretaries of State. This program responds to constituent correspondence and requests from  

[16:2:66,671] the public and advocates in the Legislature, administers the Secretary's role as a member of the National Association of  

[16:3:66,681] Secretaries of State, in the management of task forces and advisory committees, in the implementation of new federal and  

[16:4:66,692] state statutory requirements, and coordinates and disseminates information about the Office and its initiatives to the public.  

[16:5:66,702] This program also monitors elections cybersecurity incidents and promotes transparency in alerting the public regarding false  

[16:6:66,712] election websites and information as well as providing oversight on cybersecurity risk management.   It also provides the Office

[7:0:243,332] 0950   State Treasurer  

[7:1:66,354] The State Treasurer, a constitutionally established office, provides banking services for state government with goals to  

[8:0:66,364] minimize interest and service costs and to maximize yield on investments. The Treasurer is responsible for the custody of all  

[8:1:66,374] monies and securities belonging to or held in trust by the state; investment of temporarily idle state monies; administration of  

[8:2:66,384] the sale of state bonds, their redemption and interest payments; and payment of warrants or checks drawn by the State  

[8:3:66,394] Controller and other state agencies.

[8:0:66,355] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:1:66,375] 0740010 - INVESTMENT SERVICES  

[9:0:66,395] The Investment Division is responsible for investment of state monies from the date of receipt through the date of redemption.  

[9:1:66,405] During the 2018-19 fiscal year, this Division handled 8,649 security investment transactions totaling $394.7 billion. The Pooled  

[9:2:66,415] Money Investment Board (PMIB) program accounted for 7,225 of these transactions totaling $360 billion; time deposits  

[9:3:66,426] accounted for 1,139 transactions totaling $27.9 billion. The remaining $7.2 billion is invested on behalf of the state's special  

[9:4:66,436] funds, such as those associated with the California Housing Finance Agency, the Department of Fish and Wildlife, the state's  

[9:5:66,446] retirement system, etc. The Division also administers the Local Agency Investment Fund (LAIF), a voluntary investment  

[9:6:66,456] program created to offer California local agencies greater access to the financial markets through the PMIB program. In the  

[9:7:66,466] 2018-19 fiscal year, 2,405 local agencies participated in LAIF, with deposits averaging $21.7 billion for the fiscal year.  

[9:8:66,484] 0740019 - CENTRALIZED TREASURY AND SECURITIES MANAGEMENT  

[10:0:66,502] In 1949, the California Legislature amended Government Code Section 16305 to create the Centralized Treasury System  

[10:1:66,512] (CTS) thereby requiring agencies of the State to deposit their money in trust with the Treasurer. The legislation also requires  

[10:2:66,522] the Treasurer to safeguard the money and make safe and prudent investments. In 1955, the Legislature created the PMIB,  

[10:3:66,532] giving the Board the responsibility to designate the amount of money available for the investment in securities, bank deposits,  

[10:4:66,543] and loans to the General Fund.  

[11:0:66,560] The Centralized Treasury and Securities Management Division (CTSMD) oversees all banking aspects of the CTS. The goal of  

[11:1:66,570] the CTSMD is to maximize the earning of interest consistent with safe and prudent treasury management, and to ensure that  

[11:2:66,581] the depository banks provide the state with proper and adequate security for the deposit of state monies. The Treasurer  

[11:3:66,591] maintains demand bank accounts with eight banks for the purpose of providing necessary statewide depository coverage for  

[11:4:66,601] the remittance of funds collected by the various state agencies.  

[12:0:66,619] The CTSMD 1) monitors the cash flow of all state funds, forecasts cash balances, revenue, expenditures, and the amounts  

[12:1:66,629] available for daily investments, 2) ensures accurate and timely agency deposits, 3) administers and executes the wire transfer  

[12:2:66,639] of funds, 4) reconciles state accounts with depository banks and redeems all state items submitted by presenting banks for  

[12:3:66,649] payments, 5) executes the clearance and income collection for state investments (excluding PERS and STRS) and securities  

[12:4:66,660] pledged to the state, 6) fulfills the clearance and settlement of securities pledged to the state for the time, demand, and other  

[12:5:66,670] state agency programs, and 7) is responsible for the safekeeping of securities and other personal property owned by or  

[12:6:66,680] pledged to the state.  

[13:0:66,698] 0740028 - PUBLIC FINANCE

[3:0:66,83] The Public Finance Division is responsible for selling State of California general obligation bonds, commercial paper notes,  

[3:1:66,93] revenue anticipation notes, lease revenue bonds, revenue bonds, and any other indebtedness for all state agencies. The  

[3:2:66,103] Division provides debt administration services for most state bonds and is responsible for disseminating information to  

[3:3:66,113] bondholders through the Investor Relations Program.  

[4:0:66,134] The Division also assures compliance with federal tax laws applicable to certain state debt so there is no adverse  

[4:1:66,144] consequences to bondholders or increased borrowing costs to the state. The post-issuance tax compliance   includes monitoring  

[4:2:66,154] the use of bond proceeds, managing rebate and yield restriction compliance, coordinating necessary financial disclosure, and  

[4:3:66,164] ensuring proper record keeping.  

[5:0:66,182] 0740035 - ADMINISTRATION AND INFORMATION SERVICES  

[6:0:66,200] The Administration Division, Executive Office, and the Information Services Division provide executive direction and support  

[6:1:66,210] services to programs in the State Treasurer's Office. Services include budgeting, personnel, accounting, information systems,  

[6:2:66,220] business services, technical support, and production operations.

[12:0:66,552] 0780 - GOLDEN STATE SCHOLARSHARE COLLEGE SAVINGS TRUST PROGRAM  

[13:0:66,570] The Golden State ScholarShare College Savings Trust Program is California's state-sponsored 529 college savings plan  

[13:1:66,580] established to help families save for higher education.   Earnings are tax-free when used for qualified higher education expenses  

[13:2:66,591] (such as tuition, fees, supplies, books, computer equipment, and certain room and board expenses) at eligible educational  

[13:3:66,601] institutions.  

[14:0:66,618] 0785 - GOVERNOR'S SCHOLARSHIP PROGRAMS  

[15:0:66,636] The Governor's Scholarship Programs (GSP) rewarded public school students who demonstrated high academic achievement  

[15:1:66,646] with scholarships.   Students may have earned multiple $1,000 Governor's Scholars Awards and a one-time $2,500 Governor's  

[15:2:66,657] Distinguished Mathematics and Science Scholars Award for scores attained on tests taken in 2000, 2001, and 2002. GSP  

[15:3:66,667] became inoperative and was repealed after 2002.   The ScholarShare Investment Board administers scholarship awards that  

[15:4:66,677] were already earned.

[9:0:134,393] 0956   California Debt and Investment Advisory Commission  

[9:1:66,415] The mission of the California Debt and Investment Advisory Commission is to support and improve the practice of public  

[9:2:66,425] finance in California by providing responsive and reliable information, analysis, and training. The Commission assists California  

[9:3:66,435] state and local governments to monitor, issue, and manage public debt and to safely and prudently invest public funds.  

[10:0:66,455] The Commission consists of nine members including the State Treasurer, who serves as chairperson; the Governor or, upon

[10:2:66,476] Treasurer; two members of the Assembly appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly; and two members of the Senate

[6:0:66,336] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,355] 0800 - CALIFORNIA DEBT AND INVESTMENT ADVISORY COMMISSION  

[7:0:66,376] The Commission's primary objective is to enhance the knowledge of public officials with respect to the administration and  

[7:1:66,386] issuance of public debt and the investment of public funds. The Commission achieves this objective by performing functions in  

[7:2:66,396] three principal areas, including:  

[8:0:65,414] • Data Collection and Analysis - Serves as a clearinghouse of debt issued by California public entities and nonprofit student  

[8:1:76,424] loan corporations.  

[9:0:65,440] • Continuing Education - Provides educational seminars, workshops, and conferences to public officials on municipal debt and  

[9:1:76,451] public fund investment topics. In addition, the Commission provides technical assistance to public officials and taxpayers  

[9:2:76,461] through direct interaction and public forums to disseminate relevant information.  

[9:3:65,477] • Policy Research - Undertakes original research on the issuance and administration of public debt and on the investment of  

[9:4:76,487] public funds. Research results are published in the form of reports, issue briefs, or articles and are disseminated in printed  

[9:5:76,497] and electronic forms.  

[10:0:66,538] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[7:0:165,328] 0959   California Debt Limit Allocation Committee  

[7:1:66,349] The California Debt Limit Allocation Committee's mission is to allocate tax-exempt, private activity bond authority for the State  

[7:2:66,359] of California. Private activity bonds may be used by the private sector for projects and programs that provide a public benefit,  

[7:3:66,369] such as the creation of affordable housing.  

[8:0:66,390] The federal government limits the total amount of tax-exempt private activity bond authority that can be issued on an annual  

[8:1:66,400] basis. Except for the Qualified Public Educational Facility Bond Program, the bond authority limit (debt limit) is calculated by  

[8:2:66,410] multiplying the state population by $105. California's limit totaled over $4.1 billion in 2019. (California's limit for the Qualified  

[8:3:66,420] Public Educational Facility Bond Program is calculated separately by multiplying the state population by $10, and totaled $396  

[8:4:66,431] million for 2019.)  

[9:0:66,451] The Committee's allocation of tax-exempt bond authority results in the issuance of bonds by cities, counties, joint powers  

[9:1:66,461] authorities and state agencies. The bonds are purchased and used by the private sector and are not an obligation of the state  

[9:2:66,471] or federal government.  

[10:0:66,492] The Committee administers five active programs that are funded through the allocation and issuance of tax-exempt private  

[10:1:66,502] activity bonds.   The Committee is funded on a fee-supported basis and is comprised of the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the  

[10:2:66,512] Governor, or upon his designation, the Director of Finance, and the State Controller.

[10:0:66,508] 0810 - CALIFORNIA DEBT LIMIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE  

[11:0:66,528] To lower the cost of financing, specified entities can issue various bonds, including mortgage revenue bonds (MRBs) that  

[11:1:66,538] support below-market interest rate mortgage loans; and mortgage credit certificates (MCCs) that reduce a homebuyer's federal  

[11:2:66,548] tax liability. Below is a summary of each program:  

[12:0:66,569] Qualified Residential Rental Project Program - Tax-exempt housing revenue bonds lower the cost for developers of multifamily  

[12:1:66,579] rental housing, to acquire land and construct new housing, or purchase and rehabilitate existing housing. The developers  

[12:2:66,589] produce affordable rental housing for low-income households by reducing rental rates charged to these individuals and  

[12:3:66,599] families. To qualify, developers must elect either to reserve at least 20% of the units for households earning up to 50% AMI or  

[12:4:66,610] reserve at least 40% of the units for households earning up to 60% AMI. Projects that receive an award of bond authority can  

[12:5:66,620] apply for non-competitive four-percent tax credits using the California Debt Limit Allocation Committee/California Tax Credit  

[12:6:66,630] Allocation Committee Joint Application.  

[13:0:66,650] Single-Family Housing Program - Tax-exempt MRBs or MCCs to assist first-time homebuyers with purchasing homes.  

[13:1:66,661] Homebuyers may purchase single-family homes, either freestanding or detached, condominiums, or townhouses. Program  

[13:2:66,671] participants must meet income limits and must purchase a home that falls within the program's purchase price limitations.  

[14:0:66,691] Industrial Development Bond Project Program - Small-Issue industrial development bonds are tax-exempt private activity bonds  

[14:1:66,701] issued to assist manufacturing facilities finance capital expenditures. These bonds offer interest rate savings to small and  

[14:2:66,712] midsize manufacturers in contrast to conventional loans, and help manufacturers retain and create new jobs within their  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[4:0:157,155] 0964   California Transportation Financing Authority  

[4:1:66,176] The California Transportation Financing Authority was established by Chapter 474, Statutes of 2009, to increase the  

[4:2:66,186] construction of new capacity or improvements for the state transportation system in a manner that will help achieve the state's  

[4:3:66,196] goals of reducing greenhouse gas, improving air quality, and conserving natural resources.  

[5:0:66,217] The Authority consists of seven members: the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the Director of the Department of Finance, the  

[5:1:66,227] State Controller, the Director of Transportation, the Executive Director of the California Transportation Commission, a local  

[5:2:66,237] agency representative appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules, and a local agency representative appointed by the  

[5:3:66,247] Speaker of the Assembly.

[12:0:66,493] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[12:1:66,513] 0820 - CALIFORNIA TRANSPORTATION FINANCING AUTHORITY  

[13:0:66,533] The Authority was established to assist transportation agencies in obtaining financing to develop transportation projects. To  

[13:1:66,543] meet this objective, statutes allow the Authority to issue, or to approve specified project sponsors to issue revenue bonds to  

[13:2:66,553] fund transportation projects backed in whole or in part, by various revenue streams of transportation funds (including toll  

[13:3:66,564] revenues). Statutes provide the authority to approve the imposition and collection of tolls on proposed transportation projects  

[13:4:66,574] under certain conditions. The planning, programming, and allocation of transportation projects are performed by the California  

[13:5:66,584] Transportation Commission and the California Department of Transportation, as appropriate.  

[14:0:96,621] 0965   California Industrial Development Financing Advisory Commission  

[14:1:66,643] The California Industrial Development Financing Advisory Commission created employment opportunities and supported local  

[14:2:66,653] economic development by approving local entities' issuance of industrial development bonds. These bonds provided  

[14:3:66,663] manufacturers with a low-cost financing option to build, expand, or equip their facilities in California. The Commission  

[14:4:66,673] independently reviewed bond applications to ensure compliance with federal tax law and state law, provided technical  

[14:5:66,684] assistance to bond issuers, and approved the bond sales by local authorities.  

[15:0:66,704] The State Treasurer served as chairperson of the Commission. The other members   were the Director of the Department of

[11:0:166,592] 0968   California Tax Credit Allocation Committee  

[11:1:66,613] The mission of the California Tax Credit Allocation Committee is to fairly allocate federal and state tax credits to create and  

[11:2:66,624] maintain safe, quality affordable rental housing for low-income households in California. The Committee does this by forming  

[11:3:66,634] partnerships with developers, investors and public entities.  

[12:0:66,654] The Committee assists development of rental housing projects for low-income families and monitors these projects for years  

[12:1:66,664] after they are placed in service to ensure compliance with federal and state tax credit program requirements of the Committee.  

[12:2:66,675] Coordinating with state and local housing fund providers, and with private investors, the Committee helps to create and  

[12:3:66,685] maintain a supply of quality, affordable housing.  

[13:0:66,705] The Committee consists of seven members, including five voting members and two advisors. The voting members are the  

[13:1:66,715] Treasurer (Chairperson of the Committee), the Governor (who may choose the Director of Finance as his or her  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:0:66,181] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,201] 0840 - CALIFORNIA TAX CREDIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE  

[7:0:66,221] The Federal Program  

[8:0:66,242] Congress authorized the federal Low-Income Housing Tax Credit (LIHTC) program in 1986. It replaced traditional housing tax  

[8:1:66,252] incentives, such as accelerated depreciation, with a tax credit that enables developers of affordable rental housing to raise  

[8:2:66,262] project equity through the "sale" of tax benefits to investors. The federal per-capita tax credit ceiling is calculated annually and  

[8:3:66,272] indexed for inflation. 

[9:0:66,293] Two types of federal tax credits are available, generally referred to as 9-percent and 4-percent credits. These terms refer to the  

[9:1:66,303] percentage of a project's "qualified basis" an investor in LIHTC projects may deduct from his or her federal income tax liability  

[9:2:66,313] annually in each of ten years. A project's qualified basis is the portion of the total project cost used to calculate the amount of  

[9:3:66,323] the tax credit and typically excludes non-depreciable costs such as the purchase of land. The affordable housing project  

[9:4:66,333] sponsor uses or sells ten times the project's tax-credit allocation amount because investors can take the annual tax credit each  

[9:5:66,344] year for a ten-year period.  

[10:0:66,361] The federal per-capita tax credit ceiling for 9-percent credits is calculated annually and indexed for inflation.   For 2019, each  

[10:1:66,371] state has an annual housing credit ceiling of $2.76 per   state resident.   Additionally, each state may qualify annually for a share  

[10:2:66,382] of unused credits in a national pool.  

[11:0:66,399] Developments financed with tax-exempt bond proceeds may receive the 4% federal tax credit. The sponsors of such projects  

[11:1:66,410] must apply to the Committee and must conform to applicable federal and state statutory and regulatory requirements, but there  

[11:2:66,420] is no annual cap on the amount of credit that may be awarded by the state to such developments.  

[12:0:66,437] Under federal law, credit projects must remain affordable for at least 30 years. However, California's program generally requires  

[12:1:66,448] maintaining affordability for 55 years. Land use agreements are recorded against each credit project to ensure compliance.  

[13:0:66,476] The State LIHTC Program  

[14:0:66,496] In 1987, recognizing the high cost of housing in California, the Legislature authorized the state's program to augment the  

[14:1:66,506] federal program. Housing projects receiving (or that have previously received) an allocation of federal tax credits may apply for  

[14:2:66,516] an allocation of state tax credits. Projects serving farmworkers may apply for state tax credits regardless of their federal tax  

[14:3:66,527] credit status.  

[15:0:66,547] The annual state credit ceiling is indexed for inflation, and for 2019, was $100.4 million. Investors take the state tax credit  

[15:1:66,557] annually over a four-year period in contrast to the ten-year federal period.  

[16:0:66,575] Chapter 159, Statutes of 2019, authorized the California Tax Credit Allocation Committee to issue $500 Million in state tax  

[16:1:66,585] credits to be paired with the 4% federal program to bolster new construction of low income housing.  

[17:0:66,605] Farmworker Housing Program  

[18:0:66,626] Chapter 521, Statutes of 2008, folded the previous Farmworker Housing Assistance Tax Credit program into the general state  

[18:1:66,636] LIHTC program as a $500,000 annual set-aside in support of farmworker housing. Pursuant to Chapter 372, Statutes of 2017,  

[18:2:66,646] these credits differ from other state credits in that the credit percentage for tax-exempt bond financed projects is higher and  

[18:3:66,656] projects may receive state credits even if they receive a federal tax credit basis increase.  

[19:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:0:88,184] 0971   California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing  

[5:1:279,198] Authority  

[5:2:66,219] The California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing Authority was established by Chapter 908, Statutes  

[5:3:66,230] of 1980, to promote the prompt and efficient development of energy sources which are renewable or which more efficiently  

[5:4:66,240] utilize and conserve scarce energy resources. Recognizing the importance of developing a secure energy future to protect the  

[5:5:66,250] environment and ensure economic stability, the Authority advances the state's goals of reducing greenhouse gas emissions by  

[5:6:66,260] providing financing options to assist industries in increasing the deployment of sustainable and renewable energy sources,  

[5:7:66,270] implementing measures that increase the efficiency of the use of energy, creating high quality employment opportunities, and  

[5:8:66,281] lessening the state's dependence on fossil fuels. To support these goals, the Authority provides financing and credit  

[5:9:66,291] enhancements to promote the establishment of facilities that use alternative methods and sources of energy, and facilities  

[5:10:66,301] needed for the development and commercialization of advanced transportation technologies.  

[6:0:66,321] The Authority consists of five members: the State Treasurer, who serves as the chairperson, the State Controller, the Director  

[6:1:66,332] of the Department of Finance, the Chairperson of the State Energy Resources Conservation and Development Commission,  

[6:2:66,342] and the President of the Public Utilities Commission.

[6:0:66,373] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[7:0:66,393] 0850 - ALTERNATIVE ENERGY AND ADVANCED TRANSPORTATION FINANCING AUTHORITY  

[8:0:66,413] Financial assistance can take the form of loans, loan loss reserves, interest rate reductions, proceeds of bonds issued by the  

[8:1:66,423] authority, bond insurance, loan guarantees or other credit enhancements, contributions of money, or a combination thereof, as  

[8:2:66,434] determined and approved by resolution of the Authority.  

[9:0:66,454] In 2010, the Authority launched a sales and use tax exclusion (STE) program for advanced transportation and alternative  

[9:1:66,464] source manufacturing in California (Chapter 10, Statutes of 2010) and subsequently, Chapter 677, Statutes of 2012, expanded  

[9:2:66,474] the STE program to include advanced manufacturing, with an annual cap of $100 million available for STE awards. Chapter  

[9:3:66,485] 768, Statutes of 2015, further expanded the program to also include equipment primarily used to process recycled feedstock  

[9:4:66,495] and equipment that primarily utilizes recycled feedstock in the production of another product.   In 2019, Chapter 690, Statutes of  

[9:5:66,505] 2019, extended the STE program sunset date to January 1, 2026, and Chapter 672, Statutes of 2019, expanded the job  

[9:6:66,515] creation-related criteria by which CAEATFA must evaluate applications. The objective of this program is to promote the creation  

[9:7:66,525] of California-based manufacturing, businesses, and jobs that are aimed at reducing greenhouse gases, air and water pollution,  

[9:8:66,536] and energy consumption.  

[10:0:66,556] Legislation in 2010 (Chapter 15, Statutes of 2010), 2011 (Chapter 9, Statutes of 2011, First Extraordinary Session), and 2013  

[10:1:66,566] (Chapter 356, Statutes of 2013), authorized financial assistance to encourage energy efficiency retrofits. The Authority  

[10:2:66,576] developed a loan loss reserve program to assist financial institutions in making loans to homeowners in the state for residential  

[10:3:66,587] whole house energy efficiency and renewable energy projects, and developed a risk mitigation program for residential Property  

[10:4:66,597] Assessed Clean Energy programs in California.  

[11:0:66,617] The Budget Act of 2014 authorized administration of the California Hub for Energy Efficiency Financing on behalf of, and in  

[11:1:66,627] collaboration with, the California Public Utilities Commission. These energy efficiency financing pilot programs   employ various  

[11:2:66,638] types of credit enhancements to encourage and leverage private capital lending   (in both the residential and commercial  

[11:3:66,648] sectors).   The pilot programs also lower costs and expand access to capital for Californians making   energy efficiency  

[11:4:66,658] improvements needed to help achieve the state's   energy efficiency goals.

[9:0:151,490] 0974   California Pollution Control Financing Authority  

[10:0:66,511] California Pollution Control Financing Authority is committed to stimulating local economies in California by making capital more  

[10:1:66,522] accessible to small businesses, and delivering innovative financing for projects that protect and restore the environment. The  

[10:2:66,532] Authority was created to assist the solid waste, recycling, water, and wastewater industries through its Pollution Control Tax-

[10:3:66,542] Exempt Bond Program. Over the last twenty-five years, the Authority has evolved to provide financing assistance to California's  

[10:4:66,552] small business sector through its California Capital Access Program (CalCAP), and to promote the reuse and redevelopment of  

[10:5:66,562] brownfields through the California Recycle Underutilized Sites Program (CALReUSE).  

[11:0:66,583] The Authority consists of the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the State Controller, and the Director of the Department of  

[11:1:66,593] Finance.

[9:0:66,455] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:0:66,474] 0860 - POLLUTION CONTROL TAX-EXEMPT BOND PROGRAM  

[11:0:66,494] The objective of this program is to provide bond financing to California businesses, irrespective of company size, for the  

[11:1:66,504] acquisition, construction, or installation of qualified pollution control, waste disposal, water furnishing, wastewater treatment,  

[11:2:66,515] waste recovery facilities, and the acquisition and installation of new equipment. Tax-exempt financing issued by the Authority  

[11:3:66,525] assists municipalities in complying with waste diversion mandates of the California Integrated Waste Management Act of 1989.  

[11:4:66,535] As of June 30, 2019, bonds totaling approximately $16.1 billion have been issued by the Authority.  

[11:5:66,553] 0865 - CALIFORNIA CAPITAL ACCESS PROGRAM FOR SMALL BUSINESSES  

[12:0:66,573] The objective of this program is to encourage banks and other financial institutions to make loans to small businesses. CalCAP  

[12:1:66,583] for Small Businesses is a form of loan loss recovery that may provide up to 100 percent coverage on certain loan defaults. By  

[12:2:66,594] participating in CalCAP, lenders have available to them a proven financing mechanism to meet the financing needs of  

[12:3:66,604] California's small businesses. The program works through the creation of a loan loss-reserve fund for each participating  

[12:4:66,614] financial institution. The Authority funds this reserve together with the financial institution and the borrower. Additional  

[12:5:66,624] incentives are provided to lend to businesses located in specified communities. The reserve serves to reduce loan-loss risk,  

[12:6:66,634] allowing banks to lend to targeted California small businesses.  

[13:0:66,652] Prior to 2010, CalCAP was entirely funded with $38 million transferred from CPCFA's Small Business Assistance Fund (SBAF)  

[13:1:66,662] established by fees collected from large companies financed through CPCFA's Pollution Control tax-exempt bond program.   In  

[13:2:66,672] October 2010, Chapter 731, Statutes of 2010, appropriated $6 million General Fund to CalCAP to increase lending efforts.   The  

[13:3:66,683] $6 million appropriation of   the State-funded program account was fully-expended by the end of 2018 allowing the annual  

[13:4:66,693] recapture of contributions to become the primary source for the State's contributions.  

[14:0:66,713] In addition, in 2011 California was awarded an allocation of federal funds in the amount of $168 million from the federal State  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 240 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — LJE   238 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:116,29] 0974   California Pollution Control Financing Authority - Continued 

[3:0:66,83] Small Business Credit Initiative (SSBCI). The allocation was shared between the Authority, $85 million, and   the Governor's  

[3:1:66,93] Office of Business and Economic Development (Go-BIZ), $83   million.   These funds enabled the Authority to expand the  

[3:2:66,103] availability of its CalCAP for Small Business program statewide.   The Authority also launched the   Collateral Support Program   to  

[3:3:66,113] assist small businesses with more substantial capital needs.   The federal funds   were expended by the fourth quarter of 2018. 

[3:4:66,124] Funds are being   recaptured annually to sustain both the CalCAP for Small Business and the Collateral Support programs.  

[4:0:66,144] Utilizing the CalCAP model, the Authority has partnered with the California Air Resources Board (ARB) to assist diesel truck  

[4:1:66,154] and equipment owners in meeting new clean air requirements by directing a total of $167.9 million in Air Quality Improvement  

[4:2:66,164] Program funds towards the purchase or retrofit of diesel trucks to comply with ARB's Statewide Truck and Bus Rule. The  

[4:3:66,175] Authority has also partnered with the California Energy Commission to implement a $2 million pilot program to provide credit  

[4:4:66,185] enhancements and rebates to small business borrowers who install electric vehicle charging stations.  

[5:0:66,203] 0870 - CALIFORNIA RECYCLE UNDERUTILIZED SITES PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,223] The CALReUSE program assists with the reuse and redevelopment of underutilized properties with real or perceived  

[6:1:66,233] contamination issues. CALReUSE addresses a funding and information gap in the development of contaminated properties  

[6:2:66,243] (brownfields) to help bring these properties into productive reuse. Beginning in 2000, the CALReUSE Assessment Program  

[6:3:66,254] provided forgivable loans of up to $300,000, which was later increased to $500,000 per brownfield site. The funds assisted with  

[6:4:66,264] brownfield site assessment and characterization, technical assistance, and the development of remedial action plans. Eligible  

[6:5:66,274] projects included sites with potential beneficial reuse not currently redeveloped due to lack of information about real or  

[6:6:66,284] perceived contamination, uncertainty about clean-up costs, or concerns regarding time frames and the regulatory process.  

[7:0:66,305] Additionally, Proposition 1C, the Housing and Emergency Shelter Trust Fund Act of 2006, included provisions to fund  

[8:0:66,315] brownfield cleanup that resulted in the expansion of the CALReUSE Program. The CALReUSE Remediation Program received  

[8:1:66,325] $60 million in Proposition 1C funds and provided loans and grants up to $5 million per project   for   brownfield remediation that  

[8:2:66,335] promotes affordable infill residential and mixed-used developments. All CALReUSE Program funds have been awarded. The  

[8:3:66,345] CALReUSE Program's $60 million investment in cleanup of contaminated sites will result in 5,439 housing units in 30 California  

[8:4:66,356] communities.  

[9:0:66,373] 0875 - ALTERNATIVE FINANCING PROGRAMS  

[10:0:66,391] Under its authority to provide alternative methods of financing facilities for pollution control, clean water supply and alternative  

[10:1:66,401] energy production, the Authority is developing alternative financing models to assist sister agencies with achieving the state's  

[10:2:66,411] environmental goals. The Authority is authorized to receive and accept contributions from other sources including federal and  

[10:3:66,422] state agencies to carry out the purposes of its statutory authority.  

[11:0:66,439] 0876 - CALIFORNIA CAPITAL ACCESS PROGRAM FOR COMPLIANCE WITH THE AMERICANS WITH DISABLITIES ACT  

[12:0:66,460] The objective of this program, created by Chapter 787, Statutes of 2015, is to help small businesses comply with the federal  

[12:1:66,470] Americans with Disabilities Act and increase access for their employees and customers by encouraging lenders and other  

[12:2:66,480] financial institutions to make loans to very small businesses to finance tenant improvements. The Legislature provided the  

[12:3:66,490] Authority an appropriation of $10 million effective January 1, 2016, to administer a credit enhancement program following the  

[12:4:66,500] CalCAP model and create loan loss reserve accounts for lenders that enroll qualifying loans into the program.  

[13:0:66,518] 0877 - CALIFORNIA SEISMIC SAFETY CAPITAL ACCESS LOAN PROGRAM  

[14:0:66,539] The California Seismic Safety Capital Access Loan Program, authorized by Chapter 32, Statutes of 2016, provided a one-time  

[14:1:66,549] allocation of $10 million effective January 1, 2017 to administer a credit enhancement   program for   qualified small businesses  

[14:2:66,559] and residential property owners (including multi-unit dwellings and mobile homes registered by the California Department of  

[14:3:66,569] Housing and Community Development) for costs related to seismic retrofitting. The Program encourages banks and other  

[14:4:66,579] financial institutions to participate by creating loan loss reserve accounts for lenders that enroll qualifying loans into the  

[14:5:66,590] program.

[8:0:154,332] 0977   California Health Facilities Financing Authority  

[9:0:66,354] The mission of the California Health Facilities Financing Authority is to help eligible and credit worthy nonprofit and public  

[10:0:66,364] health facilities reduce their cost of capital, and promote health care improvement and cost containment objectives by providing

[11:0:66,392] The Authority was established by Chapter 1033, Statutes of 1979 (AB 1558), and consists of nine members: the State  

[12:0:66,402] Treasurer, the Director of the Department of Finance, the State Controller, two public members appointed by the Senate, two  

[12:1:66,412] public members appointed by the Assembly, and two public members appointed by the Governor.

[7:0:66,481] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[7:1:66,500] 0880 - CHILDREN'S HOSPITAL PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,518] In 2004, California voters approved Proposition 61, which established the Children's Hospital Program. In 2008, Proposition 3  

[8:1:66,528] established the second Children's Hospital Program. In 2018, Proposition 4 established a third Children’s Hospital Program.  

[8:2:66,539] The purpose of the three programs is to improve the health and welfare of California's critically ill children by providing a stable  

[8:3:66,549] and ready source of funds for capital improvement projects for children's hospitals. Children's Hospital Program grant funding is  

[8:4:66,559] derived from the issuance of general obligation bonds, up to $750 million under Proposition 61, $980 million under Proposition  

[8:5:66,569] 3, and $1.5 billion under Proposition 4.  

[8:6:66,587] 0885 - HEALTH FACILITIES BONDS, LOANS, AND GRANTS  

[9:0:66,607] The Authority serves as a conduit provider of tax-exempt bonds and a direct provider of financial assistance to health  

[9:1:66,617] institutions.  

[10:0:66,638] Tax-Exempt Bond Program  

[11:0:66,658] Bonds issued under this conduit program are not a debt, liability, or a pledge of the full faith and credit of the taxing power of  

[11:1:66,668] the state or any of its political subdivisions. The full faith and credit of the participating institutions are pledged for repayment of  

[11:2:66,679] the bonds. To qualify for funding, the proposed project must be a health facility, operated by a private nonprofit corporation or  

[11:3:66,689] association, city, city and county, county, or hospital district.  

[12:0:66,709] HELP II Loan Program  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:119,29] 0977   California Health Facilities Financing Authority - Continued 

[3:0:66,83] The Authority administers the Healthcare Expansion Loan Program II (HELP II) to assist small and rural health facilities in  

[3:1:66,93] obtaining financing for their capital needs. The HELP II Program provides two percent and three percent fixed interest rate  

[3:2:66,103] loans of up to $1.5 million to California's nonprofit small and rural health facilities in an efficient, timely, and cost effective  

[3:3:66,113] manner. HELP II loans may be used to purchase or construct new facilities, remodel or renovate existing facilities, purchase  

[3:4:66,124] equipment and/or furnishings, and refinance existing debt.  

[3:5:66,141] 0890 - MENTAL HEALTH WELLNESS GRANTS  

[4:0:66,159] • Investment in Mental Health Wellness Act of 2013 Grant Program 

[5:0:66,177] Chapter 34, Statutes of 2013 (SB 82), the Investment in Mental Health Wellness Act of 2013 and related legislation provided  

[5:1:66,187] $142.5 million in one-time General Fund, and $4 million in ongoing Mental Health Services Act funding to provide grants for  

[5:2:66,197] community based mental health crisis support, which may also be eligible for matching federal funding.  

[6:0:66,215] The Act established a grant program to disburse funds to California counties or to their nonprofit or public agency designees for  

[6:1:66,225] the purpose of developing mental health crisis support programs. Specifically, funds may be used to increase capacity for client  

[6:2:66,235] assistance and services in crisis intervention, crisis stabilization, crisis residential treatment, rehabilitative mental health  

[6:3:66,245] services, and mobile crisis support teams. The grants will support capital improvement, expansion and limited start-up costs.  

[7:0:66,266] • Investment in Mental Health Wellness Grant Program for Children and Youth  

[8:0:66,284] Chapter 30, Statutes of 2016 (SB 833), Section 20 created the Investment in Mental Health Wellness Grant Program for  

[8:1:66,294] Children and Youth to increase mental health services for children and youth 21 years of age and under to develop a complete  

[8:2:66,304] continuum of crisis services. Working with counties, the program funds facility acquisition, construction/renovation, equipment  

[8:3:66,314] acquisition, applicable startup or expansion costs, and limited personnel funding to develop crisis residential treatment and  

[8:4:66,324] crisis stabilization facilities, mobile crisis support teams, and family respite care facilities.  

[9:0:66,345] • Community Services Infrastructure Grants 

[10:0:66,362] Chapter 33, Statutes of 2016 (SB 843), Section 52 created the Community Services Infrastructure competitive grant program to  

[10:1:66,373] expand community alternatives to jail and prison. The program seeks to expand access to jail and prison diversion programs  

[10:2:66,383] and services for those with mental health illness, substance use disorders, or who have suffered from trauma. Working with  

[10:3:66,393] counties, the program funds facility acquisition, renovation, equipment acquisition, and applicable startup or expansion costs for  

[10:4:66,403] facilities that provide services to this population.  

[10:5:66,421] • No Place Like Home Program  

[11:0:66,439] Chapter 43, Statutes of 2016 (AB 1618) established the No Place Like Home Program (NPLH), which requires the Department  

[11:1:66,449] of Housing and Community Development (HCD) to award up to $2 billion to counties for the acquisition, design, construction,  

[11:2:66,459] rehabilitation, or preservation of permanent supportive housing for individuals living with a severe mental illness who are  

[11:3:66,469] homeless or at risk of chronic homelessness. Chapter 322, Statutes of 2016 (AB 1628) authorized CHFFA to enter into  

[11:4:66,479] contracts with HCD and further authorized CHFFA to issue up to $2 billion in taxable revenue bonds pursuant to the NPLH  

[11:5:66,490] Program. Chapter 41, Statutes of 2018 (AB 1827) placed the No Place Like Home program on the November 2018 ballot  

[11:6:66,500] (Proposition 2), where it was adopted by the voters as the No Place Like Home Act. This ratified existing law establishing the  

[11:7:66,510] No Place Like Home program as being consistent with the Mental Health Services Act approved through Proposition 63 in  

[11:8:66,520] 2004. It also ratified the issuance of up to $2 billion in previously authorized bonds.

[13:0:211,584] 0981   California ABLE Act Board  

[13:1:66,606] The California Achieving a Better Life Experience Act (ABLE) Board was established by Chapter 796, Statutes of 2015 (SB  

[13:2:66,616] 324) to create a Qualified ABLE Program. The Program will provide eligible individuals with disabilities the opportunity to save  

[13:3:66,626] private funds in tax-advantaged ABLE accounts for the purpose of supporting persons with disabilities to maintain their health,  

[13:4:66,636] independence, and quality of life.  

[14:0:66,657] The Board consists of the State Treasurer (Chair), the Director of Finance, the Controller, the Director of Developmental  

[14:1:66,667] Services, the Chairperson of the State Council on Developmental Disabilities, the Director of Rehabilitation, and the Chair of  

[14:2:66,677] the State Independent Living Council.

[10:0:66,545] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:1:66,564] 0895 - CALIFORNIA ABLE ACT BOARD  

[11:0:66,584] On December 19, 2014, President Obama signed the Stephen Beck Jr., Achieving a Better Life Experience Act of 2014, which  

[11:1:66,595] allows individuals who became blind or disabled before reaching age 26, to create tax-free savings accounts. Individuals can  

[11:2:66,605] make nondeductible cash contributions to an ABLE account in the name of a designated beneficiary with tax-free earnings.  

[11:3:66,615] ABLE account distributions are also not included in the beneficiary's income, as long as they are used for qualified disability  

[11:4:66,625] expenses. Chapter 774, Statutes of 2015 (AB 449), implements the ABLE Act in California, and directs the Board, with the  

[11:5:66,635] State Treasurer as Chair, to administer the California ABLE Program accounts on behalf of eligible individuals.  

[12:0:66,656] The Board and the California ABLE Program Trust were established by Chapter 796, Statutes of 2015 (SB 324), for the  

[12:1:66,666] purpose of creating the Program. CalABLE was officially launched in December of 2018 with the mission to meet the diverse  

[12:2:66,676] needs of our customers and their families. CalABLE’s pledge is to be customer-driven, accountable, and a trusted partner in  

[12:3:66,686] providing financial services.  

[13:0:66,704] Under the Program, a person may make contributions of up to $16,000 during a taxable year, to a designated beneficiary's  

[13:1:66,714] ABLE account to be used for the qualified disability expenses of that designated beneficiary.  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:66,83] 0910 - CALSAVERS  

[2:0:66,101] The Program provides workers access to a simple, portable, low-cost retirement savings account. Any private sector employer  

[2:1:66,111] with at least five employees that does not offer a workplace retirement savings vehicle by the statutory compliance deadline will  

[2:2:66,121] be required to provide their employees with access to the Program. The final date to do so is July 1, 2022. CalSavers launched  

[2:3:66,131] statewide on July 1, 2019, following a limited scope pilot.

[7:0:185,294] 0985   California School Finance Authority  

[7:1:66,316] The California School Finance Authority (CSFA), created in 1985, provides facilities and working capital financing to school  

[7:2:66,326] districts, community college districts, county offices of education, and charter schools. The State Treasurer serves as chair of  

[7:3:66,336] CSFA and the Superintendent of Public Instruction and the Director of Finance serve as members. CSFA has offices in Los  

[7:4:66,346] Angeles and Sacramento.  

[8:0:66,367] CSFA serves as the primary state agency for California charter schools seeking facility and working capital assistance by  

[8:1:66,377] providing access to low-cost financing through several State and federally funded programs.
