[9:0:66,387] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:1:66,406] 0918 - SMART BONDS PROGRAM  

[10:0:66,427] Chapter 1438, Statutes of 1985, as amended by Chapter 598, Statutes of 1987, established CSFA and authorized the issuance  

[10:1:66,437] of revenue bonds or other debt instruments. The proceeds from the sale of the bonds were available for loans to schools and  

[10:2:66,447] community college districts to assist with the acquisition of equipment and new school sites, construction of new facilities,  

[10:3:66,457] reconstruction of existing facilities, capital improvements, and to provide working capital. Chapter 325, Statutes of 2006 (AB  

[10:4:66,467] 2717), allows CSFA to issue debt on behalf of California charter schools for capital improvements and working capital needs.  

[10:5:66,485] 0920 - CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITIES PROGRAM  

[11:0:66,505] Chapter 935, Statutes of 2002, as amended by Chapter 587, Statutes of 2003, created the Charter School Facilities Program  

[11:1:66,516] (CSFP), which provides funding for the new construction, renovation or rehabilitation of charter school facilities. CSFA and the  

[11:2:66,526] Office of Public School Construction jointly administer the program. CSFP was funded through the Kindergarten-University  

[11:3:66,536] Public Education Facilities Bond Acts of 2002, 2004, 2006, and 2016, for a total of $1.4 billion. The program provides a 50  

[11:4:66,546] percent state subsidy for the charter school facilities project costs, with the balance of the project costs being repaid (to the  

[11:5:66,556] state) by the charter school in the form of a long-term lease. Recipient charter schools must provide site-based instruction, be  

[11:6:66,567] deemed financially sound by CSFA, and meet other program eligibility requirements.  

[11:7:66,584] 0925 - STATE CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITIES INCENTIVE GRANTS PROGRAM  

[12:0:66,605] In 2004, 2009, and 2014, CSFA was awarded grants under the United States Department of Education's State Charter School  

[12:1:66,615] Facilities Incentive Grants Program (CFDA 84.282D) to provide California charter schools with assistance for facilities costs.  

[12:2:66,625] Grant funds reimburse a charter school's costs for rent, lease, mortgage or debt service payments for existing or new facilities  

[12:3:66,635] or the costs of acquiring land and/or constructing or renovating a facility. Grants are awarded to charter schools based on  

[12:4:66,646] preference points allotted by the percentage of low-income students, percentage of overcrowding, not-for-profit status, and  

[12:5:66,656] demonstrated student performance. Schools cannot use program funds to supplant state funding.  

[12:6:66,673] 0930 - CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITY GRANT PROGRAM  

[13:0:66,694] The Charter School Facility Grant Program provides Proposition 98 General Fund grants to assist charter schools with rent and  

[13:1:66,704] lease costs. This program targets schools and communities with significant populations of economically disadvantaged  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:1:66,93] percent of their total annual facilities rent or lease costs.  

[1:2:66,111] 0935 - CHARTER SCHOOL REVOLVING LOAN FUND  

[2:0:66,131] Charter 1010, Statutes of 1976 established the Charter School Revolving Loan Fund in the State Treasury to provide loans of  

[2:1:66,141] up to $250,000 to new charter schools to assist them in meeting the purposes of the school's approved charter. The program is  

[2:2:66,152] available to any charter school that is not a conversion of an existing public school, and preference is given to schools that  

[2:3:66,162] have not completed their full charter term.

[6:0:168,228] 0989   California Educational Facilities Authority  

[6:1:66,250] The California Educational Facilities Authority (CEFA) provides qualified nonprofit higher education institutions with assistance  

[6:2:66,260] through a tax-exempt revenue bond program to reduce the costs of financing academic facilities.   CEFA also may issue bonds,  

[6:3:66,270] notes, and other forms of indebtedness for student loans to support students' costs of higher education.  

[7:0:66,291] CEFA consists of the following five members: the Director of Finance, the State Controller, the State Treasurer, and two public  

[7:1:66,301] members appointed by the Governor.

[5:0:66,181] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,201] 0940 - BOND FINANCING  

[7:0:66,218] CEFA issues tax-exempt revenue bonds to assist private educational institutions of higher learning to construct educational  

[7:1:66,229] facilities.   Because it is authorized to issue tax-exempt bonds,   CEFA may be able to provide more favorable financing terms  

[7:2:66,239] than might otherwise be obtainable.   CEFA also may include qualifying nonprofit entities as eligible program participants for the  

[7:3:66,249] construction of student and faculty housing.   Bonds issued by CEFA are not a debt, liability, or claim on the faith and credit or  

[7:4:66,259] the taxing power of the State of California or any of its political subdivisions.   The full faith and credit of the participating  

[7:5:66,269] institution is normally pledged to the payment of the bonds.   Bonds issued for this purpose are not subject to the state's "private  

[7:6:66,280] activity" bond ceiling as specified in federal law.  

[8:0:66,297] For purposes of the California Educational Facilities Act, "private college" or "private participating college" means a private  

[8:1:66,308] college that does not restrict the admission of a student based on the student's ethnicity, provided that the financing does not  

[8:2:66,318] violate constitutional provisions.  

[9:0:66,338] "Bond" means bonds, notes, debentures, securities, or other evidences of indebtedness.   This broad definition allows CEFA to  

[9:1:66,348] issue tax-exempt direct or private placement loans for colleges and universities, which may provide greater cost savings than  

[9:2:66,358] these colleges and universities might otherwise realize on a traditional bond financing.  

[10:0:66,378] 0955 - COLLEGE ACCESS TAX CREDIT FUND  

[11:0:66,398] Chapter 367, Statutes of 2014, required CEFA to administer the College Access Tax Credit Fund and allocate and certify the  

[11:1:66,408] tax credits for taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2014, and before January 1, 2017.   Chapter 22, Statutes of 2015,  

[11:2:66,419] added a requirement that CEFA continue to allocate and certify the tax credits for taxable years beginning on or after January  

[11:3:66,429] 1, 2017, and before January 1, 2018.   Chapter 527, Statutes of 2017, extended CEFA's responsibility to administer the tax  

[11:4:66,439] credits for taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2017, and before January 1, 2023.
